My daughter and I ate lunch there for the first time. Asked for Orange Chicken and another two plates.  The other two plates were what we asked for but the Orange Chicken was not right.  My daughter knows I'm allergic to seafood so she tried the orange chicken. She said, "Mom, I don't think you should have the Orange chicken because I don't think it's chicken" I saw the waitress walk by and asked her if what we ordered was chicken. She was quickly walking by and looked down at the plate and said, "Ya,Ya Chicken"  I un-peeled the orange crust from the dish and it turns out it looked like calamari or some form of fish.  Once I saw her again, I asked are you sure this is chicken because I am allergic to seafood.  She asked me why I'm allergic to seafood :( I told her that was a good question and would be sure to ask the ambulance why I was allergic once they got there.  Her eyes opened wide - she did not know that I had not tried the stuff.  Thank goodness for my daughters instinct in trying it first.

To make matters worse she went to the back kitchen and what sounded like a scuffle she returned saying she would only charge for the other 2 plates that we did eat from.  She knew it was their mistake and was apologetic. Needless to say she overcharged the other two plates.  I told her I was not leaving a tip but would pay the price she was charging but showed her the menu with the correct price. She obviously was overcharging me to make up for their mistake. I told her I would never again eat at this restaurant. Be careful what you get. I do not recommend this place at all. There are much better, cleaner places to eat Chinese food in Newark.</review>

< text>
Habitat has the best vanilla oat milk latte in Los Angeles county and I dare you to try to prove me wrong. I also love Habitat because it really has a lot of options for vegans and people who have gluten allergies. I have tried their gluten-free bagel and one of their gluten free cupcakes- both of which were amazing. I can't eat gluten because I am allergic and so I love going somewhere that has options for breakfast (and a dessert treat). Highly recommend if you are in the neighborhood!!< /text>

<rating>5</rating><text>Pleasantly surprised with their coffee.

I came here on a very early morning for some coffee and a pastry. I had a great experience and would recommend it to friends who are in the area. Parking was relatively easy since i came in at like 7:30AM so I honestly have no tips for that, but there is street parking.

It's a small little cafe with a lot of healthy and vegan options, so if you're looking for either of those then this is the perfect breakfast spot for you. They have a lot of options in terms of breakfast items and also a lot of pastries to choose from. I ordered an Iced Vanilla Latte and a chocolate croissant. Both were exceptionally delicious and that's saying a lot since you can get both of these in literally every coffee shop in Los Angeles.

I like this place a lot, it's got great coffee and there's a hipster vibe but not in a way that feels snobby.</text>< Pics>

The coffee is good, I've had a variety of their drinks, starting with my favorite a vanilla latte hot, pretty good not too sweet wich is perfect for me. <userid>101369752284015892943< /userid><Name>Kurt Kirkland</Name><date>1534718490065< /date><rating>2< /rating>< Review>
1st time visitor. I want to start out by stating that my wife and I specifically came here to try it out. We came on a Saturday afternoon, the beach was slightly overcast but the boardwalk was full of people and the weekly craft fair was set up adjacent to the outdoor seating (between the Crown Plaza and the parking garage). The point is, there were a lot of people milling about enjoying the day yet only one other couple was seated at La Cosecha's nice outdoor patio.
My wife and I frequent the Ventura boardwalk and beach area a lot to walk our dog and we had noticed this restaurant was usually not very busy. We both like Mexican food and wanted to try it out. On this day we had been down to Malibu to the Getty Villa and decided that 'today was the day' and we were going to give La Cosecha  a shot.
We walked up to the outdoor patio and were immediately greeted by an older gentlemen who seemed thrilled that we wanted to eat there. He lead us in to the interior and quickly summoned a waiter to seat us. We were provided menus and seated in an area where we could people watch and view the ocean - all very nice. The only other couple there were also seated on the patio and they were enjoying a meal and drinks.
The waiter returned and took our drink order. My wife ordered a house Margarita with no salt and I ordered a draft beer. They have a decent selection of craft beers available. We also ordered an appetizer plate - the guacamole and chips.
When the waiter returned with our drinks my wife noticed immediately that whoever had made her Margarita had begun with a salted glass as large chunks of salt were all over the outside like they had been hastily wiped off. When she tasted her drink it too was salty so she only took a sip and left it for the remainder of our stay. She has high blood pressure so purposely avoids salt. My beer was fine (tough to screw up a draft beer!).
We both remarked that when the appetizer was left at the table, the waiter didn't ask about our dinner choices - usually this is a good segue to get the meals going while the customer enjoys the appetizer. But no, our menus remained in front of us as we began to pick at the guacamole  and chips.
The chips are made on site and were light and crispy - they weren't oily or greasy and actually complimented the guacamole mix well. The only drawback I found was that the chips weren't very thick and tended to break easily when I tried to dip into the avocado mix. The presentation was nice - a generous serving of chips around a large scoop of avocado/onion/spice mix with slices of radish, red onion and diced tomatoes.
One nice touch was that another server (not our waiter) showed up with a small dish of sliced limes - he said that he felt the avocado tasted best with a sprinkle of lime juice so he thought he'd bring some over. It was a thoughtful gesture and he was right.
We began to feel like no one was going to take our dinner order. By this time we'd been sitting for about 45 minutes and no one asked if we wanted to place our dinner order or why my wife's Margarita sat untouched. No other patrons had come in to eat during our entire visit. Meanwhile, across the plaza the Aloha Steakhouse patio was hopping! Full of people, activity, noise and merriment and most importantly - people eating, drinking and having a good time. Compared to the atmosphere over there our experience was dead.
By this time I had eaten most of the chips and began to notice that the bottom layer contained mostly broken chip pieces and these were darker and more bitter than the fresher ones at the top were.
Still no waiter, still no dinner order taken so my wife and I decided that there was a reason the restaurant was so dead - the staff just didn't quite hit on all cylinders and we signaled the waiter that we were ready to go. We were disappointed as we had really hoped to find a new 'go-to' Mexican restaurant on the beach.</Review>

1 Star because I cant give Zero & they didn't even give me my pizza.

Called to place an order for delivery and they told me it would arrive in about 45 minutes. 40 minutes later (5 minutes before the quoted delivery time) they called me back telling me that turns out that I'm outside their delivery area and that they wont deliver my pizza to me but the pizza is ready now if I want to come pick it up at the price I already paid (including delivery and tip.) I declined.

The 3 issues with this entire interaction are as follows:

1.) Why didnt they let me know I was outside their delivery area when I gave them my address at initial order.

2.) Why did they wait 40 full minutes to call me back and let me know they couldn't deliver my order.

3.) How does it make any sense to offer to your customer to come pick up the order you previously agreed to deliver at the delivery price (delivery fee + tip included). That seems rather tone-deaf.

To top it all off they didn't inspire much confidence when I declined their offer to pick it up myself and requested a refund. They simply said, it'll get refunded without any sort of ETA or confirmation on their part.

I'm disappointed because I was looking forward to trying their pizza but the way they handle customer service has me thinking perhaps I didn't miss much.< /Text>

< UserId.>
110906414235209547669< /UserId.>
<Name>Edward Fernandez<//Name><date>1614658852234< /date><Rating>4</Rating>< review>
Ok so I ordered Coup De Thai for dinner. Got 2 different kinds of curry, pretty good. One was quite spicy, but the other was spot on. However, thats where the good part ends. There was some soup I ordered that was dreadful. Had to dump it asap. It was abnormally sweet. I instead opted to have some of my famous broth, which, of course, was fabulous. I also got some sticky rice. It was a bit too sticky , unfortunately. Had to use a steak knife to cut through it. I couldnt finish all of my sticky rice, so I plan to use it for an upcoming science project. < review>
Our group of four had a delicious dinner at Coup De Thai. For appetizers we had Samosas, Dragon Balls, and Lettuce Wraps. The wraps had a larb-like filling that was particularly fresh tasting and savory. For mains we had Green Curry, Singapore noodles, Bird in Herb, and Sauteed Eggplant. The curry wasn't as spicy as we hoped, but everything was very flavorful. Even the Happy hour half-priced bottle of Washington State Cabernet was decent. All in all, a tasty meal with friendly service in an outdoor dining setting that felt safe.<//review>

104065575295944634566<//user_id>
< Review>
The decor really draws you in, but the food keeps you there. We got the thai samosas, red curry with chicken, green curry with pork, white rice and brown rice, and pandan tapioca. We loved all of it. The curries are unlike what we've had at other Thai restaurants like it's a special recipe passed down from generations. We also had dragonfruit lemonade, which was unique but not amazing, and thai tea. We enjoyed the food over everything else. The portions are fairly large. The curries are entrees and the rice are sides. It is a few dollars pricier than other Thai restaurants. (Curry itself with chicken or pork is about $16 and rice was $3). Overall, if you don't mind spending a few extra dollars, I recommend Coup de Thai.< /Review>

Coup de Thai is a fantastic restaurant for those looking for a great Thai restaurant. The inside is very nice and well decorated. The atmosphere is very pleasant.  The menu offers a variety of options.

Crispiest of crispy wings! Just as I remembered it from Singapore to Boston. This spot has just enough seating for a nice dine in as well as outdoor seating. Local beers on top and plenty of TVs for the sports buffs. I definitely recommend folks to get half spicy and half soy garlic wings. I'm big on eating spicy food but jumping from one flavor to the other helps cut the heat as well as the pickled radish and coleslaw. (The boneless wings are like chicken tenders if you're into that but not my fave.) Super stoked to have this in Fresno!<//Text>

<review>The food at this Bonchon is actually good, I had no qualms about the taste and it was perfectly good fare for the price. What was alarming, however, was that one plate of the Japchae noodles with Beef took 45 minutes to get to our table. My party had started to eat at least 15 minutes before that. < text>
Where should I start?

The chicken?
The fried rice?
The bulgogi?
The servers?

Everything in this restaurant was just simply amazing.

The chicken was sweet and definitely my favorite out of all the dishes my family ordered. I can tell why their chicken is what most people sought out when going into Bonchons.

The fried rice was great, they had a few types of fried rice, plain, seafood, bulgogi, chicken, bacon, etc. My only qualm about it was that the portion size was a bit on the smaller side.

The bulgogi that I tried from a friend's plate tasted amazing. If I had a few more bites, I think it might rival the chicken.

The menu had most of the dishes you would see in Korean restaurants such as tteokbokki, japchae, kimchi, bibimbap, and my family enjoyed them all.

They have side dishes that also taste great.

The atmosphere of the restaurant was quite nice. The restaurant is small, but they had no problem seating 12 of us on a busy Sunday lunch/afternoon. Plus they had a little outside seating area.

Overall, I enjoyed our visit and my only qualm/problem with the place is that the price is a little high, but I guess that's what you pay for for delicious food!</text>

< Text>
A few items were ordered at this restaurant for my family. I ordered two beef tacos with rice and beans and they were pretty solid. The rice and beans were very tasty and the tacos were about what I expected. My kids shared a hamburger combo with fries and a drink and once again pretty solid. I tasted the hamburger and it was better than I expected. Where things went South was for my wife's plate. She ordered the combo that had an enchilada and a chile relleno. The enchilada had sauce on it that looked like mole sauce and it seemed like it had been sitting for a while. The mole sauce was not good and the whole enchilada was kind of a mess. The chile relleno I don't even know what happened with it but I think they forgot to put the sauce on top and the fried breading around it was more like a corn dog breading. It was probably the worst enchilada and chile relleno I have had in a long time and considering the staff looked all Latino I am surprised they are comfortable putting out that kind of a product. I get the impression that some items are good and some items are just not very good so order at your own risk.<//Text>

<username>Jason Sett</username><user_id>111770149487445553620< /user_id>< text>
As a SD native, I've been to a lot of hole-in-the-wall Mexican food restaurants, and I'd say they're somewhere in the 10th percentile when it comes to good mexican food. I live nearby so this place is pretty convenient, but their online menu doesn't match up with what they actually sell; apparently it's from another Los Amigos and it's linked to the wrong one...

But anyways, I always judge a Mexican food place by its California burrito, and this place has gotten it wrong every time. The biggest problem is with the cheap meat they use that still has tendons in it. That's happened multiple times to multiple people I know. But maybe it's just me and I don't like really chewy/hard to eat beef.

Their prices are also a little expensive for how cheap they appear to be. They even keep the salsa cups behind the counter so people don't take too many. I'll probably keep going here for the convenience of it, but this definitely isn't a place that's hit the spot for me. Who knows, maybe they're only good at cooking something I haven't tried yet...</text>

<username>Dave Plantz< /username><gmapID>0x80dbe79fab563689:0x984f76452bf6d82f<//gmapID>< review>
Carne asada tastes like it was marinated in cream of mushroom soup.  The burritos had lettuce.  What the heck?  Who does that?  Carne asada fries were put on styrofoam plate and microwaved to melt the cheese.   Fries burned through the plate.   Carne asada fries were just a small pile of fries with just meat and cheese.  Large drink was $2.50 and 85 cents a refill.   Salsa cups are handed out with your order, so if you like more salsa,  you have to pay extra.   Portions are small.   Food is served on thin floppy paper plates.   Food is expensive.   This place nickels and dimes you to death.   Do yourself a favor and eat in ramona township.  So many better places.  Country estates residents,  drive the 7 miles into town and get a real meal where you can sit down and relax and not have to pull your wallet out every time you need a little more soda or salsa.< /review>

I originally signed up for personal training, promised that 1) I could start immediately and 2) I could transfer the sessions to another location if I had to relocate. Unfortunately, they could follow through on neither of these things, and promised a refund.

Weeks passed, where I reached out multiple times weekly (over the phone and in writing) requesting cancellation/the refund. Every time, I was told that the manager would be made aware and handle it. Therefor, the manager was aware, and simply ignored the issue.

Last week, they charged me again for personal training.  They have now charged me ~$400 for a service I have attempted countless times to cancel. I have never used a single session with them. I eventually had to file a claim with my bank to block them from charging me.

I advise that everyone avoid this gym due to its scammy business practices. It is unfortunate, because the trainers and gym staff that I interacted with were friendly and tried their best to be helpful. I hope the location finds new management soon.< /Text>
